## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration. Classical reaction kinetics relates dA/dt to powers of A (rate laws), with possible explicit time dependence from external forcing or catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent rate with first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Catalyst deactivation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + t) (rate decreasing with time due to catalyst poisoning)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (empirical time-concentration coupling)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate law with constant source/sink)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate constants (c0 < 0) indicate consumption/decay of the species, positive indicate production
- Integer or half-integer power of A often corresponds to elementary reaction molecularity or radical chain mechanisms
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate surface adsorption or enzyme saturation limiting the rate
- Explicit time dependence in rate expressions often signals external forcing (light intensity, temperature program) rather than intrinsic kinetics
- Product terms A*(c-A) indicate autocatalytic or logistic behavior where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Squared denominators (c+A)^2 suggest competitive adsorption on catalytic surfaces (Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism)
- A rate law linear in A with a nonzero intercept (c0*A + c1) suggests a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- If dA/dt depends on t only through A(t), the system is autonomous and time should not appear explicitly in the best model
